Since message_id is unique per message, this caused the system prompt to differ on every turn, busting prefix-based prompt caches on local model providers (llama-server, LM Studio/MLX) and causing full cache rebuilds on every conversation turn.\\n• Why it matters: Cache invalidation on every turn increases latency, costs, and reduces efficiency for local models.\\n• What changed: Moved per-message identifiers from buildInboundMetaSystemPrompt() (system prompt) to buildInboundUserContextPrefix() (user context prefix). System prompt now contains only session-stable routing fields.\\n• What did NOT change (scope boundary): Other metadata fields (sender info, thread starter, forwarded message, chat history) remain unchanged. The subsequent `kickstart -k` would start a new process before port 18789 was released, leaving two competing gateway processes. The TUI then sees a flood of `run error: terminated` errors because `KeepAlive=true` keeps trying to restart the failing new process.\\n\\nReal-world trigger: manually running `launchctl unload + load` (e.g. to apply a plist edit) bypasses OpenClaw\\u0026#39;s wait logic entirely — the old process keeps the port, the new one fails, and launchd loops.\\n\\n## Root cause\\n\\n```\\nwaitForPidExit(pid)  ← polls process.kill(pid, 0) up to 10s\\n  if timeout → returns void   ← 🐛 old process may still hold the port\\n                                  next kickstart -k races with it\\n```\\n\\n## Fix\\n\\nTwo new helpers:\\n\\n| Helper | What it does |\\n|--------|-------------|\\n| `waitForPidExit(pid)` | Same poll loop, now returns `boolean` (true = gone) |\\n| `ensurePidGone(pid)` | Waits for graceful exit → SIGKILL fallback → polls 3s for kill to land |\\n\\n`restartLaunchAgent()` and `stopLaunchAgent()` both use `ensurePidGone()` so **the port is guaranteed free before the new process is started** and **`openclaw gateway stop` returns only after the process is truly dead**.\\n\\n## Sequence after fix\\n\\n```\\nbootout (SIGTERM)\\n  └─ ensurePidGone(previousPid)\\n       ├─ wait up to 10s for graceful exit  → done ✓\\n       └─ (if still alive) SIGKILL + wait 3s → done ✓\\nbootstrap + kickstart -k   ← port guaranteed free\\n```\\n\\n## Tests\\n\\n21 existing `launchd.test.ts` tests pass unchanged.\",\"state\":\"closed\",\"draft\":false,\"merged\":false,\"html_url\":\"https://github.com/openclaw/openclaw/pull/43961\",\"user\":{\"login\":\"happydog-intj\",\"id\":212984,\"profile_url\":\"https://github.com/happydog-intj\",\"avatar_url\":\"https://avatars.githubusercontent.com/u/212984?v=4\"},\"labels\":[\"gateway\",\"size: XL\"],\"head\":{\"ref\":\"fix/gateway-restart-race\",\"sha\":\"fc8a9fe5ecf0aebaba455ee9e57d2469ab63bf46\",\"repo\":{\"full_name\":\"happydog-intj/openclaw\",\"description\":\"Your own personal AI assistant. Any OS. Any Platform. That path eagerly resolves credentials from source config, but command paths like `plugins list` do not have an active gateway runtime snapshot, so SecretRefs such as `env`, `file`, or `exec` can throw before the plugin finishes loading.\\n- What changed:\\n- Added a config-only Feishu account preflight path that checks whether credential inputs are configured without resolving the SecretRef value.\\n- Switched Feishu tool registration prechecks (`chat`, `docx`, `bitable`, `drive`, `perm`, `wiki`) to use that config-only path.\\n- Kept actual credential resolution in execution/runtime paths, so runtime auth semantics stay strict.\\n- Added targeted regression tests for SecretRef-backed registration and config-only preflight behavior.\\n- What did NOT change (scope boundary):\\n- No global SecretRef provider semantics were changed.\\n- No gateway auth / token drift behavior was changed.\\n- No plugin slot-selection / validate-mode behavior was changed.\\n\\n## Change Type (select all)\\n\\n- [x] Bug fix\\n- [ ] Feature\\n- [ ] Refactor\\n- [ ] Docs\\n- [ ] Security hardening\\n- [ ] Chore/infra\\n\\n## Scope (select all touched areas)\\n\\n- [ ] Gateway / orchestration\\n- [ ] Skills / tool execution\\n- [ ] Auth / tokens\\n- [x] Integrations\\n- [ ] API / contracts\\n- [x] UI / DX\\n- [ ] CI/CD / infra\\n\\n## Linked Issue/PR\\n\\n- Fixes #37633\\n- Supersedes #47016\\n\\n## User-visible / Behavior Changes\\n\\n- `openclaw plugins list` no longer reports `feishu failed during register ... unresolved SecretRef ...` just because Feishu credentials are represented as SecretRefs in config.\\n- The Feishu plugin now loads on config-inspection / CLI paths as long as the credential inputs are configured.\\n- Actual credential resolution still happens when a Feishu tool executes or runtime paths start, so genuine missing/unavailable secrets still fail in the correct execution context.\\n\\n## Security Impact (required)\\n\\n- New permissions/capabilities? pattern — each API call fetches a fresh token instead of caching a potentially stale value\\n- `User-Agent` header on all outbound HTTP requests\\n- Wire Teams `clientInfo` timezone into the agent system prompt\\n\\n### AI UX Features\\n\\n- **AI-generated label**: All outbound messages include the `AIGeneratedContent` entity and `channelData.feedbackLoopEnabled` so Teams renders the \\\\\\\"AI generated\\\\\\\" badge and native thumbs up/down UI\\n- **Streaming responses** (1:1 only): Uses the [Teams `streaminfo` entity protocol](https://learn.microsoft.com/en-us/microsoftteams/platform/bots/streaming-ux) with `onPartialReply` to progressively update messages as the LLM generates tokens, throttled at 1.5s via the shared `draft-stream-loop`\\n- **Informative status updates**: Sends a randomized status message (e.g. \\\\\\\"Scuttling through ideas...\\\\\\\") immediately when a message arrives, showing a blue progress bar while the LLM processes\\n- **Typing indicators**: Only sent in group chats (Teams doesn't support them in channels; 1:1 uses streaming instead)\\n- **Welcome card**: Sends an Adaptive Card with configurable prompt starters when the bot is added to a 1:1 chat\\n- **Feedback with reflective learning**: Handles `message/submitAction` invoke for thumbs up/down. Negative feedback triggers a fire-and-forget background reflection — the agent reviews its response, derives a learning, and proactively messages the user with adjustments. Feedback events persisted as `type: \\\\\\\"custom\\\\\\\"` / `event: \\\\\\\"feedback\\\\\\\"` in session JSONL for mining\\n\\n### Infrastructure\\n\\n- `updateActivity` REST helper and `updateActivity` on `MSTeamsTurnContext` for streaming\\n- `invokeResponse` handling — no-op in custom adapter (HTTP 200 sent by `process()`)\\n- Stream fallback for long replies (\\u003e4000 chars) — falls through to chunked delivery\\n- Stream finalization for empty text (clears progress bar when agent sends a card via tool)\\n- Shared `AI_GENERATED_ENTITY` constant extracted to `ai-entity.ts`\\n- New config fields: `welcomeCard`, `promptStarters`, `groupWelcomeCard`, `feedbackEnabled`, `feedbackReflection`, `feedbackReflectionCooldownMs`\\n\\n### Bug Fix\\n\\n- **Copy-pasted image downloads**: Added `smba.trafficmanager.net` to `DEFAULT_MEDIA_AUTH_HOST_ALLOWLIST` — pasted images arrive via Bot Framework attachment URLs at this host and require the bot's Bearer token, which was previously not sent because the host was missing from the auth allowlist\\n\\n### Known Issues\\n\\n- Proactive send from DM may route to wrong conversation when user has multiple conversations (#51947)\\n\\nCloses #51806\\n\\n## Manual test evidence\\n\\nTested on Azure VM deployment with Teams Web. 29/30 tests passed, 0 failed, 1 not tested (group chat). #51824\\n\\n## Problem\\n\\nWhen switching models in the Control UI, the model picker sends the **wrong provider prefix**. For example, selecting DeepSeek from a session running on ZAI produces `zai/deepseek-chat` instead of `deepseek/deepseek-chat` — causing \\\"model not allowed\\\" errors.\\n\\nThis is the root cause behind 9+ independent bug reports across different provider combinations (ZAI/DeepSeek, Ollama/Moonshot, MiniMax/Kimi, etc.).\\n\\n## Root cause\\n\\nThree call sites use `resolveServerChatModelValue(model, modelProvider)` which blindly prepends the session's current provider to the bare model name:\\n\\n1. `ui/src/ui/app-render.helpers.ts:542` — active session model display\\n2. `ui/src/ui/app-render.helpers.ts:549` — default model display\\n3. `ui/src/ui/chat/slash-command-executor.ts:158` — /model slash command\\n\\nThe `modelProvider` from the server reflects the **previous** model's provider, not the newly selected model's provider.\\n\\n## User impact\\n\\nEvery user who switches between models from different providers in the Control UI gets \\\"model not allowed\\\" errors. Affects all multi-provider setups.\\n\\n## Fix\\n\\nFor bare model names (no `/`), create a raw `ChatModelOverride` and resolve the correct provider through `normalizeChatModelOverrideValue()`, which looks up the model in the catalog and returns the catalog's provider. Falls back to server-provided provider only if catalog lookup fails.\\n\\nAll 3 call sites are fixed. 2 files, +30/-7.\\n\\n## How to verify\\n\\n1. Configure 2+ providers (e.g. ZAI + DeepSeek)\\n2. Start a session with one provider's model\\n3. Switch to another provider's model via UI dropdown\\n4. Before: \\\"model not allowed\\\". After: switches correctly.\\n\\n## Tests\\n\\n`chat-model-ref.test.ts` covers `normalizeChatModelOverrideValue` catalog lookup. The fix routes through this existing tested path. No new test needed — the functions are correct, only the call sites were wrong.\\n\\n🤖 Generated with [Claude
